Since Šobi is characterized as a Gentile, the implication here is that Barzilai also was a Gentile and this is used to explain why some 500 years later Barzilai’s descendants could not serve as priests.</i> convert in the name of Heaven<sup class="footnote-marker">24</sup><i class="footnote">I. e., were honest converts to be counted as Jews.</i> or not<sup class="footnote-marker">25</sup><i class="footnote">A conversion for the only purpose of being able to be married to a Jewish partner is considered to be invalid; the person so converted then remains Gentile. The Babli disagrees; a conversion is valid and irrevocable if it satisfies the minimal legal conditions imposed on the act: <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yevamot 24b" href="/Yevamot.24b"><i>Yebamot</i> 24b</a>; <i>Seder Eliahu Rabba</i> Chap. 29.</i> in the name of Heaven? If you say that they converted in the name of Heaven should not [their descendants] eat most holy sacrifices? But if you say that they converted not in the name of Heaven, then [their descendants] should not eat even outside <i>sancta</i>. Even if you say that they converted in the name of Heaven, is a female proselyte not like a prostitute for the priesthood<sup class="footnote-marker">26</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 21:7" href="/Leviticus.21.7"><i>Lev</i>. 21:7</a> forbids only a whore, a desecrated woman, and a divorcee as marriage partners to the Cohen. Now the divorcee and the desecrated are Jewish born; they cannot be proselytes. The legal definition of a “whore” is a person who had sexual relations with a man whom she could not possibly marry. Since a Gentile is excluded from preliminary marriage, a Gentile woman who is presumed to have had sexual experience when very young, automatically qualifies as whore under this definition.</i>? Explain it that they were not daughters but daughters of daughters<sup class="footnote-marker">27</sup><i class="footnote">The daughters of Barzilai married not priests but courtiers of David’s court (<a class="refLink" data-ref="I Kings 2:7" href="/I_Kings.2.7"><i>1K</i>. 2:7</a>). Then their children were regular Israelites according to <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Kiddushin 3:12:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Kiddushin.3.12.1">Mishnah 3:14</a> and could marry priests.</i>. But if they were daughters of daughters, they are like Israel!<sup class="footnote-marker">28</sup><i class="footnote">Their descendants then would have been genuine priests able to serve in the Temple.</i> But following Rebbi Simeon, since Rebbi Simeon said, a proselyte who converted at less that three years and one day of age<sup class="footnote-marker">29</sup><i class="footnote">This sentence is obviously incomplete; one must add “may marry into the priesthood”, cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Bikkurim 1:5:2-4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Bikkurim.1.5.2-4"><i>Bikkurim</i> Halakhah 1:5</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yevamot 60b" href="/Yevamot.60b">Babli <i>Yebamot</i> 60b</a>, <i>Qiddušin</i> 76b,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 78a" href="/Kiddushin.78a">78a</a>.</i>. She had no intent to immerse herself but [her mother] immersed her, if then later she immerses herself for the holiness of Israel, each of them then becomes a proselyte and a proselyte is like a prostitute for the priesthood<sup class="footnote-marker">30</sup><i class="footnote">This explains the attitude of the rabbis who oppose R. Simeon. They agree that by biblical standards, the proselyte toddler could be married to a priest as explained by R. Simeon in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Bikkurim 1:5:2-4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Bikkurim.1.5.2-4"><i>Bikkurim</i> Halakhah 1:5</a>. But they require a conscious act for a rabbinically valid conversion and this is impossible for a toddler. If later the adolescent girl immerses herself for the impurity of menstruation, this is a conscious act and counts fully as valid conversion (cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Kiddushin 3:12:9" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Kiddushin.3.12.9">Halakhah 3:14, Note 278</a>.) But at that time, the girl is much older than three years and R. Simeon’s argument does not apply. It follows that the daughters of Barzilai, even if converted as toddlers, were rabbinically prohibited to priests. The priests who married them, presumably for their money and standing at court, therefore created a class of rabbinically desecrated priests who could be barred from Temple <i>sancta</i> (in the formulation of G) but not from outside <i>sancta</i>.</i>.
Any person who converts because of love, i. e., a man because of a woman or a woman because of a man, or proselytes of the king’s table<sup class="footnote-marker">31</sup><i class="footnote">People who convert in order to obtain a government post.</i>, or lion proselytes<sup class="footnote-marker">32</sup><i class="footnote">The ancestors of the Samaritans who converted because of fear of the lions (2<i>K</i>. 17:25 ff.)</i>, or the proselytes of Mordechai and Esther<sup class="footnote-marker">33</sup><i class="footnote">“And many of the people of the land became Jewish, for the fear of the Jews fell on them” (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Esther 8:17" href="/Esther.8.17"><i>Esth</i>. 8:17</a>).</i>, one does not accept. Rav said, they are proselytes<sup class="footnote-marker">34</sup><i class="footnote">This is rabbinic practice.</i>; one does not reject them in the way one has to reject proselytes from the start<sup class="footnote-marker">35</sup><i class="footnote">A person who wants to become Jewish has to be told that he is better off not being a Jew (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Yevamot 47b" href="/Yevamot.47b">Babli <i>Yebamot</i>47b</a>) and sent away; he can be accepted only if he comes back.<br>This is the translation of the text of L. The text is problematic since שֶׁמָּא “perhaps” is Babylonian Aramaic. According to G, one has to read: “They have to be approached a second time, to convert them for the name [of Heaven].” While the text of L represents rabbinic practice from the Middle Ages, the text of G has no echo in rabbinic literature. Therefore, the text of L has to be preferred.</i>. But one accepts them; they need to be received in a friendly way; perhaps<sup class="footnote-marker">36</sup><i class="footnote">One continues to prove that in fact all categories of people enumerated in the Mishnah were among the returnees from the Babylonian captivity.</i> they became proselytes for God<sup class="footnote-marker">24</sup><i class="footnote">I. e., were honest converts to be counted as Jews.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">36</sup><i class="footnote">One continues to prove that in fact all categories of people enumerated in the Mishnah were among the returnees from the Babylonian captivity.</i>“Proselytes,” meaning “everyone who separated himself from the impurities of the peoples of the earth to join them.<sup class="footnote-marker">37</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezra 6:21" href="/Ezra.6.21"><i>Ezra</i> 6:21</a>. In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 70a" href="/Kiddushin.70a">Babli, 70a</a>, the verse is applied to both proselytes and freedmen.</i>” Freedmen, as in “and all the Gibeonites, etc.<sup class="footnote-marker">38</sup><i class="footnote">G shows that the reference is to <a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezra 2:58" href="/Ezra.2.58"><i>Ezra</i> 2:58</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Nehemiah 7:60" href="/Nehemiah.7.60"><i>Neh</i>. 7:60</a>; the freedmen are the “sons of Solomon’s servants” mentioned in that verse. In both cases, MT is without initial ו.</i>” Bastards. Rebbi Simeon said, it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">39</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezra 2:60" href="/Ezra.2.60"><i>Ezra</i> 2:60</a> = <a class="refLink" data-ref="Nehemiah 7:61" href="/Nehemiah.7.61"><i>Neh</i>. 7:61</a>. The subject are people for whom it is questionable whether they should be able to contract Jewish marriages. The place names have not been identified. A similar homiletic interpretation of the same verse is in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 70a" href="/Kiddushin.70a">Babli, 70a</a>.</i>: “And the following came up from Salt Hill, Ploughing Hill”. From Salt Hill, that is Babylon. Ploughing Hill refers to silenced ones and foundlings<sup class="footnote-marker">40</sup><i class="footnote">“Ploughing” as metaphor for illicit sexual activity is hinted at in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Judges 14:18" href="/Judges.14.18"><i>Jud</i>. 14:18</a>. In Karaite theory, the forbidden ploughing on the Sabbath (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 34:21" href="/Exodus.34.21"><i>Ex</i>. 34:21</a>) is the sex act.</i>. Kerub<sup class="footnote-marker">41</sup><i class="footnote">As in the interpretation of <i>Cherubim</i> as “like youngsters”, represented as baby angels, כ is taken as prefix, not part of the root.</i> means the bastards; the young are those who go after their eyes<sup class="footnote-marker">42</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sotah 1:8:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sotah.1.8.1"><i>Soṭah</i> Mishnah 1:8</a>.</i>; Addon<sup class="footnote-marker">43</sup><i class="footnote">Reading the place name אַדּוֹן as noun אָדוֹן.</i>, for they were saying, there is no judgment and no Master. Rebbi Ḥizqiah changed the wording: These are those who went after their eyes and said, there is no judgment and no judge. And Immer<sup class="footnote-marker">44</sup><i class="footnote">Accadic/Aramaic אמר “lamb”, homiletically identified with Hebrew המר (in Galilean pronounciation which identified א ה ח ע) “to rebel” (cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 107:11" href="/Psalms.107.11"><i>Ps</i>. 107:11</a>).</i>, who rebelled against God by their evil deeds. Rebbi Abbun in the name of Rebbi Phineas: They publicized themselves like the seam of a garment<sup class="footnote-marker">45</sup><i class="footnote">Identifying אמר “lamb” and Aramaic/Syriac אִמְרָה (חוּמְרָא) “knot, seam, flounce”, in addition to Hebrew אִמְרָה “maxim, saying”. The sermon uses <i>Immer</i> as acoustic echo of all these meanings.</i>. Rebbi Levi in the name of Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish: They would have been worthy of being turned into a salt hill, but Divine justice was silent for them. Ploughing Hill.
<sup class="footnote-marker">48</sup><i class="footnote">To this and the following paragraph there exists an almost parallel text in <i>Sanhedrin</i> 6:9 (ן), an enlarged version in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yevamot 78b-79a" href="/Yevamot.78b-79a">Babli <i>Yebamot</i> 78b–79a</a> and <a class="refLink" data-ref="Bamidbar Rabbah 8:4" href="/Bamidbar_Rabbah.8.4"><i>Num</i>.<i>rabba</i> 8(4</a>), and a shortened version in <i>Midrash Samuel</i> 28[5].</i>[“The dedicated ones”]<sup class="footnote-marker">49</sup><i class="footnote">Reading of G; in L: “It was stated”. The following text deals with the identity of “the dedicated ones”, their exclusion from the Jewish marriage community, and proof that they were among the returnees from Babylon.</i>. Rebbi Immi in the name of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi, because of: “At that moment Joshua <i>dedicated them</i> as hewers of wood and drawers of water for the congregation.<sup class="footnote-marker">50</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Joshua 9:27" href="/Joshua.9.27"><i>Jos</i>. 9:27</a>.</i>” One understands “for the congregation.” But “for the Eternal’s altar”<sup class="footnote-marker">51</sup><i class="footnote">This is also mentioned in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Joshua 9:27" href="/Joshua.9.27"><i>Jos</i>. 9:27</a>, but the service in the Tabernacle is reserved for priests and Levites. The statement is interpreted to mean that their status will only be determined when the Eternal’s altar is given its permanent place.</i>? But Joshua kept them in limbo. He said, I shall not include nor exclude them. But he who sometime in the future will build the Temple, if he wants to include them he may include, exclude them he may exclude. David came and excluded them as it is said<sup class="footnote-marker">52</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 21:2" href="/II_Samuel.21.2"><i>2S</i>. 21:2</a>.</i>: “But the Gibeonites are not part of the Children of Israel.” Why did he exclude them? Because “<sup class="footnote-marker">53</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 21:1" href="/II_Samuel.21.1"><i>2S</i>. 21:1</a>.</i> there was a famine in David’s time, three years year after year.” David said, for four sins<sup class="footnote-marker">54</sup><i class="footnote">In ן “three” and this also seems to be the reading underlying the Babli’s version and <i>Pirqe R</i>.<i>Eliezer</i> Chapter 17. The number is 4 in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Taanit 3:3:2-6" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Taanit.3.3.2-6"><i>Ta‘anit</i> 3:3</a> (66c 1. 29).</i> the rains are locked away. For the sins of foreign worship, incest and adultery, murder, and the sins of those who publicly promise money for welfare but do not pay. From where for the sin of foreign worship? “<sup class="footnote-marker">55</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 11:16-17" href="/Deuteronomy.11.16-17"><i>Deut</i>. 11:16–17</a>.</i> Beware, lest you be seduced” etc. What is written afterwards? “The Eternal’s rage will be inflamed against you and he locks the sky, etc.” From where for the sins of the incestuous and adulterers? “<sup class="footnote-marker">56</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jeremiah 3:2-3" href="/Jeremiah.3.2-3"><i>Jer</i>. 3:2–3</a>. While the prophet obviously speaks of Baal worship, all his imagery is that of sexual transgressions. Quoted in the name of R. Jehudah in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sifra, Kedoshim, Chapter 7 4" href="/Sifra,_Kedoshim,_Chapter_7.4"><i>Sifra Qedošim Pereq</i>7(4</a>).</i> You distorted the Land by your immorality and your evil deeds.” What is the punishment? “Rainshowers were withheld, there was no late rain,” etc. From where because of the murderers? “<sup class="footnote-marker">57</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 35:33" href="/Numbers.35.33"><i>Num</i>. 35:33</a>.</i> Because blood will distort the Land.” From where for the sins of those who publicly promise money for welfare but do not pay? “<sup class="footnote-marker">58</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Proverbs 25:14" href="/Proverbs.25.14"><i>Prov</i>. 25:14</a>. In the name of different Amoraim in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Taanit 8b" href="/Taanit.8b">Babli, <i>Ta‘anit</i>8b</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Proverbs 25:14" href="/Proverbs.25.14"><i>Midrash Prov</i>. 25(14</a>).</i> Clouds and wind but no rain means the man who prides himself by lying gifts.” David checked his entire generation and did not find one of these. He turned to ask the <i>urim</i> and <i>tummim</i>. That is what is written: “<sup class="footnote-marker">53</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 21:1" href="/II_Samuel.21.1"><i>2S</i>. 21:1</a>.</i> David asked before the Eternal” by <i>urim</i> and <i>tummim</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">59</sup><i class="footnote">In MT, there is a lacuna in <a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 21:1" href="/II_Samuel.21.1"><i>2S</i>. 21:1</a> between “David asked before the Eternal,” and “The Eternal said, because of Saul and the House of blood guilt.” It is explained that he asked by applying the <i>urim and tummim</i> oracle. In the Babli and the sources dependent on it, R. Eleazar explains that “asking <i>before</i> the Eternal” means applying the <i>urim and tummim</i> oracle since in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 27:21" href="/Numbers.27.21"><i>Num</i>. 27:21</a> it says, “<i>before</i> Eleazar the priest he shall stand and ask the <i>urim and tummim</i>.”</i> Rebbi Eleazar said, “Ask the Eternal, all the meek of the Land, who execute His Law.<sup class="footnote-marker">60</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Zephaniah 2:3" href="/Zephaniah.2.3"><i>Zeph</i>. 2:3</a>. The homily is slightly more explicit in the Babli, where it is credited to R. Simeon ben Laqish. It addresses a seeming inconsistency in <a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 21:1" href="/II_Samuel.21.1"><i>2S</i>. 21:1</a> where God’s answer is that the famine is a punishment for two crimes, the first “about Saul” and the second “about the House of blood guilt because he killed the Gibeonites.” The verse of the prophet is read to mean that even at the moment a person is judged for his misdeeds his “works”, his good deeds, are mentioned in the Heavenly court. But here the sin “about Saul” was not Saul’s but David’s and the entire people’s since they let him be buried in Transjordan and did not bring him to his proper burial in his ancestral land until prodded by the absence of rain (<a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 21:14" href="/II_Samuel.21.14"><i>2S</i>. 21:14</a>, where the coming of rain is described as a direct consequence of the proper burials given to Saul and Jonathan.)</i>” What means “Whose Law is Work”? He enforces His Law and this is His Action<sup class="footnote-marker">61</sup><i class="footnote">While the Babli certainly reads with the Masoretes פָּעָלוּ, it might be that the Yerushalmi reads פָּעֳלוֹ.</i>. “<sup class="footnote-marker">53</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 21:1" href="/II_Samuel.21.1"><i>2S</i>. 21:1</a>.</i> The Eternal said, because of Saul and the House of blood guilt.” “Because of Saul,” whom you did not grant the last favor, “and because of the House of blood guilt, for he had killed the Gibeonites.” David sent and called them, what is between you and the house of Saul? They told him, because he killed seven of our men, two hewers of wood, two drawers of water, a religious leader, a scribe, and a beadle. He asked them, what do you want now? They said to him: “<sup class="footnote-marker">62</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 21:6" href="/II_Samuel.21.6"><i>2S</i>. 21:6</a>.</i> May there be given to us seven men of his sons and we shall hang them before the Eternal on the hill of Saul, the elected of the Eternal.” He said to them, what use is it for you that they be killed? Take silver and gold for yourselves! But they answered, <sup class="footnote-marker">63</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 21:4" href="/II_Samuel.21.4"><i>2S</i>. 21:4</a>.</i>“there is no money for us from Saul and his house.” He said, maybe they are afraid<sup class="footnote-marker">64</sup><i class="footnote">In ן: They are afraid one in front of the other (to accept blood money).</i>; he separated them and spoke to each one separately, trying to mollify him by himself, and asked him: What use is it for you that they be killed? Take gold and silver! But he said, “there is no money for us from Saul and his house.” It is written “for me”<sup class="footnote-marker">65</sup><i class="footnote">In <a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 21:4" href="/II_Samuel.21.4"><i>2S</i>. 21:4</a>, the <i>Ketib</i> is “for me” but the <i>Qere</i> “for us”. The homily explains both readings; both are correct.</i>. At this moment, David said that the Holy One gave three good gifts to Israel: They are merciful, decent, and charitable<sup class="footnote-marker">66</sup><i class="footnote">In addition to the sources mentioned in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Kiddushin 4:1:7" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Kiddushin.4.1.7">Note 48</a>, the following is also in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 1" href="/Psalms.1"><i>Midrash Psalms</i> 1</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 17" href="/Psalms.17">17</a>.</i>. From where that they are merciful? “He gave you mercy<sup class="footnote-marker">67</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 13:18" href="/Deuteronomy.13.18"><i>Deut</i>. 13:18</a>.</i>.” From where that they are decent? “That His fear should be on your faces.<sup class="footnote-marker">68</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 20:20" href="/Exodus.20.20"><i>Ex</i>. 20:20</a>.</i>” This is a sign, for a decent person does not sin. About anybody indecent it is clear that his ancestors did not stand on Mount Sinai. From where that they are charitable? “The Eternal, your God, kept for you covenant and charity.<sup class="footnote-marker">69</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 7:12" href="/Deuteronomy.7.12"><i>Deut</i>. 7:12</a>.</i>” But these, nothing of this in found in them. Immediately he went to exclude them as it is said: “But the Gibeonites are not of the Children of Israel.<sup class="footnote-marker">52</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 21:2" href="/II_Samuel.21.2"><i>2S</i>. 21:2</a>.</i>” And Ezra also excluded them, as it is said: “And the dedicated ones dwelt in the Ophel.<sup class="footnote-marker">70</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Nehemiah 3:26" href="/Nehemiah.3.26"><i>Neh</i>. 3:26</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Nehemiah 11:21" href="/Nehemiah.11.21">11:21</a>. The emphasis is on their dwelling separately.</i>” Also in the future the Holy One, praise to Him, will exclude them as it is written: “One crossing the city they cause to be lost.<sup class="footnote-marker">71</sup><i class="footnote">This quote (as well as the version of G) is clearly corrupt; it telescopes a quote and its interpretation into one sentence. The correct text is in ן:<br>וְהָעוֹבֵד הָעִיר יַעַבְדוּהוּ מִכֹּל שִׁבְטֵי יִשְׂרָאֵל.<br>יַאֲבִידוּהוּ מִכֹּל שִׁבְטֵי יִשְׂרָאֵל.<br>(<a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 48:19" href="/Ezekiel.48.19"><i>Ez</i>. 48:19</a>) “The city worker will cultivate it, from all the tribes of Israel.” (Interpretation) ‘He will cause him to be lost from all the tribes of Israel.’<br>Ezechiel, in his description of the future Israel, gives Jerusalem a strip of land from the Meditteranean to the Dead Sea, which will be cultivated by the Temple workers to provide food for the city. The verse is taken out of context and, in Galilean dialect, ע and א are identified, changing “cultivate” into “getting lost”. The city worker is the dedicated one.</i>”
It is written: “The King said, I shall give<sup class="footnote-marker">73</sup><i class="footnote">Here ends the Genizah fragment.</i>.” “The King took the two sons of Riṣpah bat Ayah whom she had born to Saul, Admoni and Mephiboshet<sup class="footnote-marker">74</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 20:8" href="/II_Samuel.20.8"><i>2S</i>. 20:8</a>. In the MT ארמני, not אדמוני. The verse ends: “And the five sons of Mikhal, Saul’s daughter, which she had borne to Adriel ben Barzilai from Meḥolah.” Adriel’s wife was Merab, Saul’s elder daughter (<a class="refLink" data-ref="I Samuel 18:19" href="/I_Samuel.18.19"><i>1S</i>. 18:19</a>).</i>,” etc. “Michal, Saul’s daughter, did not have a child until the day of her death,<sup class="footnote-marker">75</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 6:23" href="/II_Samuel.6.23"><i>2S</i>. 6:23</a>. In the opinion of the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sukkah 5:4:2-4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sukkah.5.4.2-4">Yerushalmi (<i>Sukkah</i> 5:4</a>, 55c 1. 22; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sanhedrin 2:4:2-5" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sanhedrin.2.4.2-5"><i>Sanhedrin</i> 2:4</a>, 20b 1. 57) she died in childbirth. In the opinion of the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sanhedrin 21a" href="/Sanhedrin.21a">Babli (<i>Sanhedrin</i> 21a</a>) she earlier had a child in Hebron.</i>” and you say so? Say now that they were sons of Merab but Michal raised them, so they were named after her. “He gave them into the hand of the Gibeonites who hanged them on the mountain before the Eternal; all seven fell together.<sup class="footnote-marker">76</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 20:9" href="/II_Samuel.20.9"><i>2S</i>. 20:9</a>.</i>” Defective without י<sup class="footnote-marker">77</sup><i class="footnote">In the MT, the word is written with an extra  י, שבעתים,correctly spelled in G and ן. The correct text seems to that of G and ן: “One is missing”, referring to Mephiboshet ben Jonathan.</i>. That refers to Mephiboshet ben Jonathan ben Saul, who was great in the Torah and David intended to save him from their hand. David said, I let them pass by the altar and anyone received by the altar will be mine. He let each pass by the altar, prayed for him, and the altar moved and received him. This is what is written: “I shall call to the Most High God, to the Power Who has the ultimate decision about me<sup class="footnote-marker">78</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 57:3" href="/Psalms.57.3"><i>Ps</i>. 57:3</a>.</i>!” For the Holy One, praise to Him, agreed with David. “<sup class="footnote-marker">76</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 20:9" href="/II_Samuel.20.9"><i>2S</i>. 20:9</a>.</i> They were killed on the first days of harvest;” it is written “the barley harvest.” “Riṣpah bat Ayah took a sack and laid it out on the rock.<sup class="footnote-marker">79</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 20:10" href="/II_Samuel.20.10"><i>2S</i>. 20:10</a>.</i>” What means: “On the rock”? Rebbi Hoshaia said, she was reciting: “The rock, perfect is His action<sup class="footnote-marker">80</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 32:4" href="/Deuteronomy.32.4"><i>Deut</i>. 32:4</a>, the verse which opens the traditional burial service called צִדּוּק הַדִּין “justification of the (Divine) judgment.” This is alluded to not only here (and in the sources mentioned in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Kiddushin 4:1:7" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Kiddushin.4.1.7">Note 48</a>) but also in the Babli, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Avodah Zarah 18a" href="/Avodah_Zarah.18a"><i>‘Avodah zarah</i> 18a</a>.</i>.” Rebbi Abba bar Zamina in the name of Rebbi Hoshaia: Sanctification of the Name is greater than desecration of the Name. Referring to desecration of the Name it is written: “Do not leave his corpse on the gallows overnight.<sup class="footnote-marker">81</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 21:23" href="/Deuteronomy.21.23"><i>Deut</i>. 21:23</a>.</i>” But referring to sanctification of the Name it is written: “From the start of harvest until water was poured on them.<sup class="footnote-marker">79</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 20:10" href="/II_Samuel.20.10"><i>2S</i>. 20:10</a>.</i>” This teaches that they were hanging from the sixteenth of Nisan<sup class="footnote-marker">82</sup><i class="footnote">The first day of the barley harvest, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 23:14" href="/Leviticus.23.14"><i>Lev</i>. 23:14</a>.</i> to the seventeenth of Marḥeshwan<sup class="footnote-marker">83</sup><i class="footnote">The year is declared one of draught if the rains did not start by the 17th of <i>Marḥeshwan</i> (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Taanit 1:3:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Taanit.1.3.1">Mishnah <i>Ta‘anit</i>1:4</a>).</i>. The passers-by were saying: How did these people sin that the rules of justice were changed for them? They were answered: Because these had attacked attached<sup class="footnote-marker">84</sup><i class="footnote">The word was changed by the corrector. Probably one should read with אֲרוּרים ן “cursed”, <i>Jos</i>. 9:33.</i> proselytes. They would say that even for those who did not convert for the sake of Heaven, the Eternal avenged their blood; if one would convert for the sake of Heaven not so much more? There is no Power like your God and no people like your people. Many converts were converted at that time; that is what is written<sup class="footnote-marker">85</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Chronicles 2:16-17" href="/II_Chronicles.2.16-17"><i>2Chr</i>. 2:16–17</a>.</i>: “Solomon counted all proselytes and appointed from them 70’000 carriers and 80’000 hewers of stone in the mountains.”
Rav Huna said that in the days of Rebbi Eleazar ben Azariah they tried to include them<sup class="footnote-marker">86</sup><i class="footnote">To permit marriage with Gibeonites.</i>. Rebbi Abbahu inverts the wording: In the days of Rebbi Eleazar they said, who could purify the altar’s part<sup class="footnote-marker">87</sup><i class="footnote">R. Eleazar ben Azariah vetoed the admission of Gibeonites into the Jewish marriage pool by arguing that <a class="refLink" data-ref="Joshua 9:23" href="/Joshua.9.23"><i>Jos</i>. 9:23</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Joshua 9:27" href="/Joshua.9.27">27</a> implies that Joshua made the Gibeonites Temple slaves, in addition to their being the people’s slaves by <a class="refLink" data-ref="Joshua 9:21" href="/Joshua.9.21"><i>Jos</i>. 9:21</a>. Now the servitude to the people had certainly lapsed. The “dedicated ones” returned from Babylonia as free men and one had to assume that already in the time of the Judges they had regularly been manumitted in this respect. But nobody could manumit Temple slaves, and marriage with slaves was impossible. In this version, the exlusion of Gibeonites from the Jewish marriage pool is a legal necessity which cannot be changed.</i>? That implies that Joshua excluded them. He excluded them only as disqualified for marriage. If you would say, disqualified (because of sins)<sup class="footnote-marker">88</sup><i class="footnote">It seems that one should read with the parallel in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Ketubot 3:1:2-19" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Ketubot.3.1.2-19"><i>Ketubot</i> 3:1</a> (27a 1. 59), <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Kiddushin 4:1:3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Kiddushin.4.1.3">Notes 16–19</a>, עבדות “slavery” instead of עבירות “sins”.</i> then the rapist of a Gibeonite girl should not have to pay the fine, but we have stated<sup class="footnote-marker">89</sup><i class="footnote">Implied by <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Ketubot 3:1:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Ketubot.3.1.1">Mishnah <i>Ketubot</i> 3:1</a>. The same Mishnah states that the statutory fine is not applicable to the rape of a virgin slave girl. If Gibeonites were excluded as Temple slaves, they should be classified with slaves in matters of the fine (and be excluded from marriage in all its forms.) Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosafot on Yevamot 79a:12:1" href="/Tosafot_on_Yevamot.79a.12.1">Tosafot <i>Yebamot</i> 79a, <i>s.v</i>. ונתינים</a>. It follows that R. Abbahu’s argument is rejected.</i>: The rapist of a Gibeonite girl has to pay the fine.” Rebbi Eleazar said, he cursed them as a snake, as it is said: “But now you are cursed<sup class="footnote-marker">90</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Joshua 9:23" href="/Joshua.9.23"><i>Jos</i>. 9:23</a>.</i>.” And it is written: “The people of Israel said to the Ḥiwwite.<sup class="footnote-marker">91</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Joshua 9:7" href="/Joshua.9.7"><i>Jos</i>. 9:7</a>.</i>” But were they Ḥiwwites<sup class="footnote-marker">92</sup><i class="footnote">In <a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 20:2" href="/II_Samuel.20.2"><i>2S</i>. 20:2</a>, they are described as Emorites.</i>? They acted like the snake<sup class="footnote-marker">93</sup><i class="footnote">In Amaraic חִוְיָא. The name of Eve, חַוָּה, instead of the Hebrew חַיָּה, hints at her relationship with the snake.</i> which said, I know that the Holy One, praise to Him, did say “because on the day you eat from it, you will die a death<sup class="footnote-marker">94</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 2:17" href="/Genesis.2.17"><i>Gen</i>. 2:17</a>.</i>.” I shall go and trick them so that they eat and will be punished and I shall inherit the earth for myself. So these people acted; they said, we know that the Holy One, praise to Him, said to Israel: “You shall certainly ban them, the Hittite, the Emorite, and the Perizite, as the Eternal, your God, has commanded you<sup class="footnote-marker">95</sup><i class="footnote">Misquoted from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 20:17" href="/Deuteronomy.20.17"><i>Deut</i>. 20:17</a>.</i>” And it is written: “You shall not conclude a covenant with them.<sup class="footnote-marker">96</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 7:2" href="/Deuteronomy.7.2"><i>Deut</i>. 7:2</a>.</i>” We shall go and trick them that they conclude a covenant with us. As you take it, if they kill us, they violate their oath. If they let us live, they violated the [divine] decision. In any case, they will be punished and we shall inherit the Land.
<sup class="footnote-marker">97</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph and the next are from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yevamot 1:6:6-7" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yevamot.1.6.6-7"><i>Yebamot</i> 1:6, Notes 229–242</a> (<b>א</b>). The full comparison of the texts of the next paragraph is given there.</i> Rav Naḥman bar Jacob said, one accepts proselytes from Kurds and Palmyrenians. Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: A Mishnah said that the proselytes from Palmyra are acceptable. There, we have stated: “All stains coming from Petra are pure.” Therefore, the proselytes from Palmyra are acceptable.
Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa presented traditions: Of Rebbi Ḥanina and Rebbi Joshua ben Levi, one declares permissible and the other admits. He who declares permissible admits. But he who admits does not declare admissible. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun in the name of Rebbi Naḥman: Babylonia, as far as family pedigree is concerned, extends up to the <i>yzq</i> canal. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, of Rav and Samuel, one said up to the <i>yzq</i> canal, the other said up to the <i>Wani</i> canal. Rav Jehudah said, between the rivers is like Nahardea as far as family pedigree is concerned. Rebbi Ḥanina ben Beroqa in the name of Rav Jehudah: The people of Moesia are questionable only because of doubts of desecrated women. The Cohanim amongst them did not care about divorcees. There they said, Moesia is dead, Media sick, Elam and <i>gbby</i> dying. The maritime district is the purple-blue of Babylonia. <i>Šny</i>’,<i>gbby</i>’,<i>and ṣrry</i> are purple-blue of the maritime district.
<sup class="footnote-marker">98</sup><i class="footnote">The following four paragraphs are from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yevamot 8:3:8-11" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yevamot.8.3.8-11"><i>Yebamot</i> 8:3, Notes 193–212</a>.</i> Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa in the name of Rebbi Josia: The eleventh generation of bastards is qualified following Rebbi Simeon; he does not use [the principle of <i>gezerah šawah</i> for] “the tenth, the tenth.” It was stated: Rebbi Eleazar ben Rebbi Simeon says, in the eleventh generation of bastards, the males are forbidden but the females permitted. Rebbi Samuel ben Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, it turns out that Rebbi Eleazar ben Rebbi Simeon follows the argument of Rebbi Meïr. As Rebbi Meïr said, a <i>gezerah šawah</i> is as if written in a verse, so Rebbi Eleazar ben Rebbi Simeon says, a <i>gezerah šawah</i> is as if written in a verse. Here also, the males are forbidden but the females permitted. In that case, even immediately? Only from the tenth onward.
They asked Rebbi Eliezer, what is the status of the eleventh generation of a bastard? He said to them, bring to me a third generation and I shall declare him pure, for he would not live. Rebbi Eliezer parallels Rebbi Ḥanina? As Rebbi Ḥanina said, once every sixty to seventy years the Holy One, praise to Him, brings a plague into the world to eliminate the bastards and he takes the qualified ones with them in order not to publicize the sinners. This parallels what Rebbi Levi said in the name of Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish: “In the place where the ascent offering has its throat cut before the Eternal, the purification sacrifice has its throat cut,” in order not to publicize the sinners. “Also He is wise and brings evil;” could one better understand “also He is wise and brings good”? But to teach you that even the evil that the Holy One, praise to Him, brings to the world, He brings in wisdom. “His word He did not remove, He overcomes the house of evildoers and accomplices of workers of iniquity.”<sup class="footnote-marker">99</sup><i class="footnote">In <i>Yebamot</i>, the statement of R. Levi in the name of R. Simeon ben Laqish is repeated here.</i><br><sup class="footnote-marker">100</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Kiddushin 3:12:2-4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Kiddushin.3.12.2-4">Chapter 3:14, Notes 242-247</a>.</i> Rav Huna said, no bastard lives more than thirty days. When Rebbi Ze‘ira immigrated here, he heard voices call “he-bastard, she-bastard”. He said, what is this? There goes that of Rav Huna, since Rav Huna said, no bastard lives more than thirty days. Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa said to him, I was with you when Rebbi Abba, Rav Huna said in the name of Rav: No bastard lives more than thirty days, when? If it is unknown. Therefore, if it is known, he lives.
Rebbi Yasa in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: In the future, the Holy One, praise to Him, will only deal with the tribe of Levi. What is the reason? “The refiner will sit, the purifier of silver, and will refine them,” etc. Rebbi Ze‘ira said, like a man who only drinks from a clean cup. Rebbi Hoshaia said, because we are not<sup class="footnote-marker">101</sup><i class="footnote">In <i>Yebamot</i>: “we are”. According to the Babli, he was a Cohen, therefore also a Levite.</i> Levites, should we lose? Rebbi Ḥanina the son of Rebbi Abbahu said, also in the future, the Holy One, praise to Him, will deal with them charitably. What is the reason? “They will be for the Eternal presenters of an offering in charity.”
Rebbi Joḥanan said, one does not investigate a family in which a family disqualification has disappeared. Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said, a Mishnah says so: “There was a family Bene Ṣerifa in Transjordan who were forcibly distanced by Ben Ṣion. Another [family] was there who were forcibly integrated by the people of Ṣion.<sup class="footnote-marker">102</sup><i class="footnote">The text of <b>ג</b> “by Ben Ṣion” is confirmed by all sources of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Eduyot 8:7" href="/Mishnah_Eduyot.8.7">Mishnah <i>Idiut</i> 8:7</a>.</i>” Nevertheless, the Sages did not want to make their names public. But the Sages transmit them to their sons and students two times in a Week. Rebbi Joḥanan said, by the Temple service, I know them and the leading personalities of the generation have disappeared in them. Rebbi Joshua ben Levi said, Pashḥur ben Immer had 5000 slaves, and their traces have disappeared in the high priesthood. These are the insolent in the priesthood. Rebbi Eleazar said, their main training: “Your people is like quarrelsome priests.” Rebbi Abbahu said, Samaritans disappeared in thirteen villages in the times of [persecution]<sup class="footnote-marker">103</sup><i class="footnote">The translation follows <b>ג</b> which alone makes sense.</i>. They said, עדן דמשאה<sup class="footnote-marker">104</sup><i class="footnote">This place is unidentified, just as is the corresponding one in <b>ג</b>.</i> is one of them.
<sup class="footnote-marker">105</sup><i class="footnote">This text is from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yevamot 8:2:2-12" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yevamot.8.2.2-12"><i>Yebamot</i> 8:2</a>, explained there in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Kiddushin 4:5:1-2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Kiddushin.4.5.1-2">Notes 150–155</a>.</i> Rebbi Ḥanina said, the Mishnah does not follow Rebbi Jehudah, since Rebbi Jehudah said that four congregations are called “congregation”, the congregation of Cohanim, the congregation of Levites, the congregation of Israelites, the congregation of converts. They objected to Rebbi Jehudah, but is it not written, “one injured in his testicles or with amputated urethra should not come into the Eternal’s congregation”? That refers to bodily blemishes. But is it not written, “children that will be born to them in the third generation may enter the Eternal’s congregation”? That is a positive commandment. But the rabbis said, there are three congregations, the congregation of Cohanim, the congregation of Levites, the congregation of Israelites; “they shall not come, they shall not come, they shall not come.”

Halakhah 2

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> What is a silenced one? Anyone who knows his mother but not his father. But a foundling is one collected from the public domain who knows neither his father nor his mother. Abba Shaul called the silenced one “investigated one”.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “What is a silenced one,” etc. What means “investigated one”? Investigate him<sup class="footnote-marker">106</sup><i class="footnote">One has to apply the rules detailed in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Ketubot 1:8:2-3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Ketubot.1.8.2-3"><i>Ketubot</i> 1:8</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Ketubot 1:9:2-5" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Ketubot.1.9.2-5">9</a> to determine whether or not the child is to be treated as a bastard. In the interpretation of the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 74a" href="/Kiddushin.74a">Babli, 74a</a>, Abba Shaul holds that the unmarried mother is to be believed if she states that the child is not the result of an incestuous relationship.</i>!
The brother of Rebbi Jehudah bar Zavdi in the name of [Rav]<sup class="footnote-marker">107</sup><i class="footnote">This is the reading later in the Halakhah, in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Bava Batra 3:1:2-7" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Bava_Batra.3.1.2-7"><i>Baba batra</i> 3:1</a>, and in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 73b" href="/Kiddushin.73b">Babli, 73b</a>, against the reading here ר׳ meaning “Rebbi”.</i>: As long as a baby lies in the public domain, either his father or his mother can testify about him<sup class="footnote-marker">108</sup><i class="footnote">As long as the baby was not taken up, it is not called a foundling and one of the parents is empowered to declare it his child and not a bastard.</i>. Once he was collected from the public domain, one needs two witnesses; its father and mother are like two witnesses<sup class="footnote-marker">109</sup><i class="footnote">Once it is designated a foundling, it needs two witnesses to admit it to the Jewish marriage pool. If two people declare that they are its parents, they really disqualify themselves as witnesses since close relatives cannot testify. Nevertheless, they are admitted <i>as if</i> they were true and independent witnesses.</i>. The rabbis of Caesarea in the name of Rav Ḥisda<sup class="footnote-marker">110</sup><i class="footnote">In <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Bava Batra 3:1:2-7" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Bava_Batra.3.1.2-7"><i>Baba batra</i> 3:1</a>, the rule is attributed directly to Rav Ḥisda. This may support S. Lieberman’s contention that Tractate <i>Neziqin</i> was edited by the rabbis of Caesarea.<br>In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 73b" href="/Kiddushin.73b">Babli, 73b</a>, Rava restricts this rule to years of famine or similar situations where the parents may be expected to be unable to care for their child.</i>: That is, if the baby is not moving. But a baby which is moving needs two witnesses; its father and mother are like two witnesses. This parallels what Rebbi Yannai said: property rights on jumping calves and lambs cannot be proven by possession<sup class="footnote-marker">111</sup><i class="footnote">If the ownership of an independently moving calf or lamb is in dispute, one cannot say that the person in whose herd it is at the moment is in possession and any other claimant has to bear the burden of proof since the animal could have wandered with the herd; the situations of both the person in possession and the claimant are equal and ownership has to be proven independently.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">112</sup><i class="footnote">The same statements are in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 73b" href="/Kiddushin.73b">Babli, 73b</a>.</i> Rebbi Abba in the name of Rav Ḥisda: Three are trustworthy immediately<sup class="footnote-marker">113</sup><i class="footnote">They are trustworthy <i>only</i> immediately; after some time they must be treated under the rules which require two independent witnesses.</i>: a midwife, a caravan, and the one who purifies her colleagues. A midwife: “The midwife took and wound a red string [around his hand] to indicate that this one was born first<sup class="footnote-marker">114</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 38:28" href="/Genesis.38.28"><i>Gen</i>. 38:28</a>, quoted incompletely. In a multiple birth, the midwife has the authority to determine which child was born first, which may determine inheritance rights. The Babli empowers the midwife to testify who is whose child in case several women give birth in the same room.</i>.” A caravan, as Rebbi Abba, the brother of Rebbi Jehudah bar Zavdi said in the name of Rav: As long as a baby lies in the public domain, either its father or its mother can testify about him. Once it was collected from the public domain, one needs two witnesses; its father and mother are like two witnesses. The one who purifies her colleagues, as we have stated there<sup class="footnote-marker">115</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Niddah</i> 9:4.</i>: “Three women sleep on one bed. If blood was found under one of them, all three are impure<sup class="footnote-marker">116</sup><i class="footnote">In the impurity of menstruation.</i>. If one of them checked herself out and found herself impure<sup class="footnote-marker">116</sup><i class="footnote">In the impurity of menstruation.</i>, she is impure and the other two are pure.” Rebbi Abba said, only within 24 hours<sup class="footnote-marker">117</sup><i class="footnote">The Babli emphatically disagrees and requires that the checking be done immediately upon leaving the bed.</i>.

Halakhah 3

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Any who are forbidden to marry in the congregation are permitted to marry one another<sup class="footnote-marker">118</sup><i class="footnote">Even a bastard who is certainly forbidden may marry a foundling whose status is only questionable, as already stated in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Kiddushin 4:1:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Kiddushin.4.1.1">Mishnah 1</a>.</i> but Rebbi Jehudah forbids. Rebbi Eliezer says, certain with certain are permitted, certain with questionable, questionable with certain<sup class="footnote-marker">119</sup><i class="footnote">This clause was inserted only as a memory help; “certain with questionable” is the same as “questionable with certain”; it does not make any difference who is the male and who the female.</i>, and questionable with questionable are forbidden. The following are questionable: the silenced one, the foundling, and the Samaritan<sup class="footnote-marker">120</sup><i class="footnote">Who are Jewish but do not follow the rabbinic rules of marriage and divorce. The child of a Samaritan divorcee from a second husband might be a bastard by rabbinic rules.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">121</sup><i class="footnote">The entire Halakhah is from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yevamot 8:2:5-9" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yevamot.8.2.5-9"><i>Yebamot</i> 8:2, Notes 136–155</a> (<b>ג</b>).</i> Rebbi Jeremiah said, as a matter of principle, an Israel with an injured testicle may marry a female bastard. Rebbi Yose said, it applies only to family disabilities, not to bodily defects. The strength of Rebbi Yose comes from the statement of Rebbi Ḥilqiah, Rebbi Simon in the name of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi: One did state this only for an Israel with an injured testicle, but not a Cohen, since, as you say there, if he is certainly a Cohen he is forbidden to marry a convert; here also, he is certainly an Israel and forbidden to marry a female bastard.
[In the opinion of Rebbi Jehudah, may a male bastard not marry a female bastard?]<sup class="footnote-marker">124</sup><i class="footnote">Missing here, added from <b>ג</b>. Since the paragraph is the answer to the question asked in this sentence, it is clear that <b>ג</b> is the source and the text here the copy.</i> Let us hear from the following, as Rebbi Immi said, Rebbi Jacob from Gebal stated before Rebbi Joḥanan, Rebbi Isaac bar Tevele in the name of Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish: Rebbi Jehudah stated that a male bastard should not marry a female bastard so that bastards should disappear from the world. Similarly, is an Ammonite man forbidden to marry an Ammonite woman? Was that needed for the rabbis? For if Rebbi Jehudah thought that this disqualified converts from any of the Eternal’s congregations, then [the Ammonite] could not marry an Ammonite woman since for her he would be of the Eternal’s congregation. He could not marry an Egyptian woman since for her he would be of the Eternal’s congregation. Rebbi Mattania said, one frees a slave girl and marries her to him. Similarly, could an Egyptian man not marry an Egyptian woman? Let us hear from the following, as Rebbi Abbahu stated before Rebbi Joḥanan: “Rebbi Jehudah said, Benjamin, an Egyptian convert, was a student of Rebbi Aqiba. He said, I am an Egyptian convert married to an Egyptian convert. My son is an Egyptian convert; I shall marry him to an Egyptian convert so that my grandson will be qualified to marry into the congregation. Rebbi Aqiba said to him, my son, it is not so. But you marry him to the daughter of an Egyptian woman convert so that there should be three generations on either side.”
Rav Jehudah in the name of Rav: Practice follows Rebbi Eliezer. The words of the Sages? Rebbi Jeremiah in the name of Rebbi Samuel bar Rav Isaac: “No bastard shall marry into the Eternal’s congregation”. He cannot marry into a congregation which is certain. He may marry if the membership in the congregation is questionable.
There, we have stated: “If it is doubtful whether [the child is] a nine-months’ child of the first [brother] or a seven-months’ of the second, he has to divorce her, the child is legitimate, and they are obligated for a reparation offering for a possible sin.” It was stated: “The first son could be [High]<sup class="footnote-marker">125</sup><i class="footnote">Missing from the text here but necessary. If the male child is legitimate and his father a Cohen, he is a Cohen. The emphasis is on the fact that the child in theory could be High Priest.</i> Priest, any second son possibly is a bastard. Rebbi Eliezer ben Jacob said, there is no such thing as a possible bastard.” Rebbi Eliezer ben Jacob agrees in cases of doubt of Samaritans and desecrated persons. This refers to what we have stated there: “Ten classes returned from Babylonia.” In the opinion of Rebbi Eliezer ben Jacob, eight. In the opinion of Rabban Gamliel and Rebbi Eliezer, nine. In the opinion of the rabbis, ten.

Halakhah 4

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> One who comes to marry a woman from a priestly family<sup class="footnote-marker">126</sup><i class="footnote">Since only in priestly families the women may become disqualified, the Cohen who wants to be sure that his descendants will be qualified to serve in the Temple is asked to verify that in generations back no divorcee or otherwise disqualified woman married into his fiancée’s family.</i> has to check four mothers who are eight: Her mother, and her maternal grandmother, her mother’s paternal grandmother and great-grandmother<sup class="footnote-marker">127</sup><i class="footnote">The list is obviously incomplete; the Mishnah in the Babli and the independent Mishnah mss. add the paternal grandmother and the latter’s mother and mother-in-law. The list is quite uneven; looking at the bride’s family tree we denote by <i>f</i> a female to be checked, by <i>m</i> a male:<br><i>f     f</i><br>׀     ׀<br><i>f  f  f</i><br>׀  ׀  ׀<br><i>f  m  f  m</i><br>׀  /  ׀  /<br><i>f     m</i><br>׀   /<br>bride<br>The positions mentioned in the Yerushalmi Mishnah are underlined.</i>. But for a levitic or Israel woman one adds another generation<sup class="footnote-marker">128</sup><i class="footnote">Even though priestly disqualifications do not apply to these women.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “One who comes to marry a woman from a priestly family,” etc. Rebbi Joḥanan said, this is Rebbi Meïr’s, as we have stated<sup class="footnote-marker">129</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Ketubot 1:9:4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Ketubot.1.9.4"><i>Ketubot</i> 1:9 (Notes 248–254</a>); a slightly different version in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Kiddushin (Lieberman) 5:2" href="/Tosefta_Kiddushin_(Lieberman).5.2">Tosephta 5:2</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Ketubot 14a" href="/Ketubot.14a">Babli <i>Ketubot</i> 14a</a>.</i>: “What is qualified dough<sup class="footnote-marker">130</sup><i class="footnote">As dough is kneaded from different ingredients, so a dough woman is descended from both more and less qualified sources; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Ketubot 1:9:3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Ketubot.1.9.3"><i>Ketubot</i>1:9 Note 251</a>. [For “mixture of dough” used as simile for lineage, perhaps also cf. Swiss-German expression <i>vom Teig</i>“from the dough”, meaning “from (the best) families”. (E.G.)]</i>? Anyone about whom there is [no suspicion of descent from] a desecrated one, a bastard, or a Gibeonite. Rebbi Meïr says, the daughter of any woman not tainted with any of these is qualified for the priesthood. But about a family in which a disability had disappeared, Rebbi Meïr says he checks up to four mothers and marries, but the Sages say, he checks forever.<sup class="footnote-marker">131</sup><i class="footnote">Until he finds the source of the trouble.</i>” Rav said, these<sup class="footnote-marker">132</sup><i class="footnote">The interpretation of the position of the Sages.</i> are the words of Rebbi Meïr, but the Sages say, he checks from which family one marries into the priesthood and marries<sup class="footnote-marker">133</sup><i class="footnote">All women in a family from whom one married into the priesthood are qualified unless her personal disqualification be known. In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 76b" href="/Kiddushin.76b">Babli, 76b</a>, Rav’s statement is stronger: A presumption of legitimacy applies to all families (unless anything derogatory be known).</i>. Through whom does he check? Rebbi Ḥaggai in the name of Rebbi Josia: He checks through his female relatives<sup class="footnote-marker">134</sup><i class="footnote">Testimony by females is close to be hearsay evidence, but sufficient to qualify a marriage. The language of the statement is derived from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Ketubot 1:9:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Ketubot.1.9.1">Mishnah <i>Ketubot</i> 1:9</a>, dealing with a woman’s bodily defects.</i>. To Rebbi Ḥama came an old man<sup class="footnote-marker">135</sup><i class="footnote">Interpretation of <i>Pene Moshe</i>.<i>Qorban Ha‘eda</i> reads: Rebbi saw an old man coming. Both interpretations are possible; in neither case is the text idiomatic Aramaic.</i>; he asked him: Does one marry into the priesthood from this family? He answered: yes, and he<sup class="footnote-marker">136</sup><i class="footnote">R. Ḥama.</i> was making a match based on this information. Rav said to his son Ḥiyya: Descend a degree to marry a wife<sup class="footnote-marker">137</sup><i class="footnote">Rav had married a noble woman and relative who gave him a hard time.</i>. Rebbi Idi said, the following is a frequent saying of the rabbis: “If the woman was not impure but she is pure.<sup class="footnote-marker">138</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 5:28" href="/Numbers.5.28"><i>Num</i>. 5:28</a>.</i>” If she was not impure, she is pure<sup class="footnote-marker">139</sup><i class="footnote">They reject the Mishnah and hold that anybody can marry any woman about whose family nothing derogatory is known.</i>. Not like Pappos ben Jehudah who locks the door before his wife<sup class="footnote-marker">140</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sotah 1:7:3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sotah.1.7.3"><i>Soṭah</i> 1:7, Note 260</a>. He did not permit his wife to talk to any male except himself.</i>. One said to him, did your forefathers act like this<sup class="footnote-marker">141</sup><i class="footnote">Jews do not lock up their wives in a harem; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sotah 1:7:2-5" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sotah.1.7.2-5"><i>Soṭah</i> 1:7</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Gittin 90a" href="/Gittin.90a">Babli <i>Giṭṭin</i> 90a</a>.</i>? A Cohen came to Rebbi Joḥanan and said to him: I acted on the Mishnah when I married a woman from a priestly family and checked after her four mothers which are eight. He said to him, if the origin was defective, who would inform you<sup class="footnote-marker">142</sup><i class="footnote">If there was a problem a few generations earlier, would you know? Note that the Cohen quotes the Mishnah in Hebrew, claiming the status of a learned person, but R. Joḥanan answers him in Aramaic, demoting him to the unlearned class since he followed the Mishnah.</i>?
“But for Levites or Israel one adds another generation<sup class="footnote-marker">143</sup><i class="footnote">This quote is different from the Mishnah which speaks of a Cohen marrying a non-priestly wife whereas here one refers to a non-priest marrying a priestly wife. The <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Kiddushin (Lieberman) 5:4" href="/Tosefta_Kiddushin_(Lieberman).5.4">Tosephta, 5:4</a>, straddles the issue, mentioning לְוִיָּה וְיִשְׂרְאֵלִים “a Levite (f. singular) and Israels (m. plural)”.</i>.” Does it not turn out that one is more stringent for an Israel than for a Cohen? <sup class="footnote-marker">144</sup><i class="footnote">In a different situation R. Yose ben R. Abun gives the same explanation in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Ketubot 1:5:2-3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Ketubot.1.5.2-3"><i>Ketubot</i> 1:5</a>, end. He seems to think that in Herodian times and later the priests had a tendency to develop into a separate caste.</i> Rebbi Yose ben Abun said, in both cases<sup class="footnote-marker">145</sup><i class="footnote">Both the cases mentioned in the Mishnah and the one mentioned in the quote.</i> the Sages demanded a fine so that everybody should cling to his tribe and family.

Halakhah 5

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> One does not investigate from the altar<sup class="footnote-marker">146</sup><i class="footnote">The daughters of priests accepted for service in the Temple are automatically qualified to be married by priests.</i> and before, or from the podium<sup class="footnote-marker">147</sup><i class="footnote">The same holds for daughters of Levitic men accepted as singers in the Temple. One has to assume that the same holds for Levites serving in other functions in the Temple.</i> and before<sup class="footnote-marker">148</sup><i class="footnote">The Babylonian Mishnah adds: “Nor from the Synhedrion and before.” This addition is unnecessary since it is implied by the next sentence.</i>. From every family whose ancestors were known as public officials and welfare administrators one marries into the priesthood; no investigation is necessary. Rebbi Yose says, also anybody signing as witness in the ancient archive<sup class="footnote-marker">149</sup><i class="footnote">Greek ἀρχεῖον. It seems that only select families were admitted to be notaries to certify deeds in Sepphoris.</i> of Sepphoris. Rebbi Ḥanina ben Antigonos says, also anyone who ever was registered in the king’s army<sup class="footnote-marker">150</sup><i class="footnote">Greek στρατία.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “One does not investigate from the altar and before,” etc. It is written<sup class="footnote-marker">151</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 17:15" href="/Deuteronomy.17.15"><i>Deut</i>. 17:15</a>.</i>: “You certainly shall put a king over you.” This refers not only to a king; from where to add public officials, administrators of welfare, clerks of the court, and those who whip with a lash<sup class="footnote-marker">152</sup><i class="footnote">Employees of the criminal court.</i>; from where? The verse says, “from amidst your brothers you shall appoint a king over you<sup class="footnote-marker">151</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 17:15" href="/Deuteronomy.17.15"><i>Deut</i>. 17:15</a>.</i>,” anybody whom you appoint over you shall only be from the select among your brethren<sup class="footnote-marker">153</sup><i class="footnote">He can be called your brother only if he belongs to your marriage group. Therefore, anybody whose daughter cannot be married by anybody, including priests, is excluded from public office. In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 76b" href="/Kiddushin.76b">Babli, 76b</a>, it is inferred from this argument that only children of a Jewish mother can be appointed to public office.</i>. Rebbi Samuel bar Naḥman in the name of Rebbi Jonathan: “Their distinguished lineage in the army in war.<sup class="footnote-marker">154</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Chronicles 7:40" href="/I_Chronicles.7.40"><i>1Chr</i>. 7:40</a>. This refers to the statement of R. Ḥanina ben Antigonos and a hypothetical army of the Messiah. In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 76b" href="/Kiddushin.76b">Babli, 76b</a>, “the king’s army” is interpreted as David’s army as described in <i>1Chr</i>.</i>” The merit of their lineage supports them in war. So far from tradition<sup class="footnote-marker">155</sup><i class="footnote">Prophets and Hagiographs, which do not have standing as sources of the law.</i>; from the words of the Torah? “No bastard shall come into the Eternal’s congregation<sup class="footnote-marker">156</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 23:3" href="/Deuteronomy.23.3"><i>Deut</i>. 23:3</a>.</i>.” “No person injured in his testicles shall come<sup class="footnote-marker">157</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 23:2" href="/Deuteronomy.23.2"><i>Deut</i>. 23:2</a>. The spelling supports the Yemenite tradition.</i>, etc.” What is written afterwards? “When you encamp against your enemies, etc.<sup class="footnote-marker">158</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 23:10" href="/Deuteronomy.23.10"><i>Deut</i>. 23:10</a>, directly after the end of the rules of exclusion from endogamous marriage. It is explicit in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yevamot 4a" href="/Yevamot.4a">Babli (<i>Yebamot</i> 4a</a>) that the order of verses in <i>Deut</i>. is important for the correct interpretation. The implication is that only persons of impeccable lineage should be admitted to the Eternal’s army.</i>”

Halakhah 6

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> The daughter of a male desecrated priest<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">Descendants of the forbidden union of a priest and a divorcee or a prostitute.</i> is always disqualified for the priesthood. The daughter of an Israel who married a desecrated woman is qualified for the priesthood<sup class="footnote-marker">159</sup><i class="footnote">Desecrated priests and their descendants can marry Israel or Levite partners without sin. According to <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Kiddushin 3:12:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Kiddushin.3.12.1">Mishnah 3:14</a>, the children have the status of the male, qualified Israel for an Israel father and desecrated priest for a desecrated father.</i>. The daughter of adesecrated priest who married an Israel woman is disqualified for the priesthood. Rebbi Jehudah says, the daughter of a male proselyte is like the daughter of a desecrated priest<sup class="footnote-marker">160</sup><i class="footnote">This statement has no basis in the Torah; it accepts as law <a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 44:22" href="/Ezekiel.44.22"><i>Ez</i>. 44:22</a> which instructs priests to marry only “virgins from the seed of Israel and widows of priests.”</i>. Rebbi Eliezer ben Jacob said, the daughter of an Israel who married a proselyte is qualified for the priesthood and the daughter of a proselyte who married an Israel woman is qualified for the priesthood, but the daughter of a proselyte who married a proselyte is disqualified for the priesthood<sup class="footnote-marker">161</sup><i class="footnote">Even if she was conceived after both partners became Jewish. He accepts as “seed of Israel” the child of either a male or a female Israel.</i>, both proselytes and freedmen, even for ten generations, unless the mother be from Israel. Rebbi Yose says, even the daughter of a proselyte who married a proselyte is qualified for the priesthood<sup class="footnote-marker">162</sup><i class="footnote">If they married after conversion, as Jews, their children are “the seed of Israel”.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “The daughter of a desecrated priest,” etc. Rav Hamnuna in the name of Rav: Daughter, daughter’s daughter, forever<sup class="footnote-marker">163</sup><i class="footnote">All descendants of a desecrated priest are desecrated, both male and female, for all generations.</i>. Rebbi Joḥanan in the name of Rebbi Ismael: “In his clans.” Since by “in his clans” said there males are forbidden and females permitted, so by “in his clans” said here males are forbidden and females permitted<sup class="footnote-marker">164</sup><i class="footnote">In <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 21:1" href="/Leviticus.21.1"><i>Lev</i>. 21:1</a> it is stated that a Cohen may not defile himself by impurity “in his clans”. A female member of a priestly family is under no such constraint. It is claimed that in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 21:4" href="/Leviticus.21.4">v. 4</a>, in which a Cohen is warned not to enter a marriage which would desecrate him, the expression “in his clans” similarly frees female members of a priestly family from the disability of desecration.</i>. What is the difference between them<sup class="footnote-marker">165</sup><i class="footnote">Rav and R. Joḥanan.</i>? A Cohen who came to a divorcee and fathered a son; the son went and fathered a son and a daughter. In the opinion of Rav the son, the son’s daughter, the daughter’s son, and the daughter are forbidden<sup class="footnote-marker">166</sup><i class="footnote">In fact, all descendants in all degrees are desecrated.</i>. In the opinion of Rebbi Joḥanan the son’s daughter is forbidden, the daughter’s son is permitted<sup class="footnote-marker">167</sup><i class="footnote">Following the Mishnah, if she married an Israel or a Levite.</i>. The Mishnah disagrees with Rav: “The daughter of an Israel who married a desecrated woman is qualified for the priesthood.” He explains it, a broomstick desecrated one<sup class="footnote-marker">168</sup><i class="footnote">Rav will hold to his position that all descendants of a desecrated priest remain desecrated and the females forbidden to the priesthood. But he notes that there is a category of desecrated women who are not descendants of desecrated priests, <i>viz</i>., women having had sexual relations with men whom they could not have married (such as women raped by Gentiles.) He will agree that the daughter of such a woman, whom he calls חֲלָלָה מְבָנָה “broomstick desecrated”, born as a regular Jew and married to an Israel, is qualified for the priesthood. (Explanation of <i>Qorban ha‘edah</i>.)<br>Since חֲלָלָה מְבָנָה does not make much sense, one might read חֲלָלָה מִבִּיאָה “desecrated by intercourse.”</i>. The Mishnah disagrees with Rebbi Joḥanan: “Rebbi Jehudah says, the daughter of a male proselyte is like the daughter of a desecrated priest.<sup class="footnote-marker">169</sup><i class="footnote">Since R. Jehudah holds that <a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 44:22" href="/Ezekiel.44.22"><i>Ez</i>. 44:22</a> prohibits the daughter of a proselyte from an Israel mother to the priesthood, how could he agree that the daughter of a desecrated woman from an Israel is qualified for the priesthood?</i>” He explains that Rebbi Jehudah only comes to add<sup class="footnote-marker">170</sup><i class="footnote">He does not disagree with the anonymous Tanna; he only comes to add rules about proselytes not mentioned by the anonymous Tanna.</i>. If he had said that the daughter of a desecrated priest is like the daughter of a male proselyte, you would have had a point.
<sup class="footnote-marker">171</sup><i class="footnote">From here to the end of the Halakhah, the text is from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yevamot 8:2:2-12" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yevamot.8.2.2-12">Yebamot 8:2</a> (<b>ג</b>), explained in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Kiddushin 4:5:2-6:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Kiddushin.4.5.2-6.2">Notes 156–164</a>; partially from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Bikkurim 1:5:2-4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Bikkurim.1.5.2-4"><i>Bikkurim</i> 1:5</a> (<b>ר</b>), <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Kiddushin 4:1:9-2:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Kiddushin.4.1.9-2.2">Notes 87–106</a>. The Leiden ms. in <i>Bikkurim</i> only notes the first few words and then writes “one continues this in <i>Qiddušin</i>4:7.” The full text was added by someone who prepared the ms. for the Venice printer; that text must have come from another ms. since not all deviations from L can be explained by copyists’ errors.</i> Example. The elder Rebbi Hoshaia and Rebbi Judah Neśia were sitting together. Rebbi Joḥanan ran und whispered into Rebbi Hoshaia’s ear: May a Cohen who is injured in his testicles marry the daughter ofconverts? He asked him, what did he tell you? He answered, a question which a carpenter, son of carpenters, cannot resolve. He did not ask me about a convert, since she is like a whore for him. He did not ask about an Israelite daughter, whom he will desecrate. He asked only about the daughter of converts! Is the daughter of converts not an Israel? You have to explain it following Rebbi Jehudah, who said, the daughter of a male convert has the status of the daughter of a desecrated male.
<sup class="footnote-marker">172</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph is not a copy of the corresponding paragraph in <i>Yebamot</i> (<b>ג</b>, Note 171).</i> If a Cohen had intercourse with a divorcee and fathered a daughter, what is the status of the daughter’s daughter<sup class="footnote-marker">173</sup><i class="footnote">Assuming the mother was married to an Israel.</i>? Rebbi Ḥanania and Rebbi Mana, one said she is qualified<sup class="footnote-marker">174</sup><i class="footnote">Following R. Joḥanan.</i>, the other said she is disqualified<sup class="footnote-marker">175</sup><i class="footnote">Following Rav.</i>. The one who said that she is qualified asked the one who said that she is disqualified: Is the daughter of a male desecrated priest not disqualified<sup class="footnote-marker">176</sup><i class="footnote">This is explicit in the Mishnah.</i>? Is the broomstick desecrated one not disqualified<sup class="footnote-marker">177</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yevamot 6:5:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yevamot.6.5.1">Mishnah <i>Yebamot</i> 6:5</a>.</i>? Why is she disqualified<sup class="footnote-marker">178</sup><i class="footnote">Since she is qualified by <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Kiddushin 3:12:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Kiddushin.3.12.1">Mishnah 3:14</a>, she does not appear in any list of disqualified women. (Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Kiddushin 4:6:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Kiddushin.4.6.2">Note 168</a>.)</i>?
“Rebbi Eliezer ben Jacob says,” etc. There, we have stated: “Rebbi Eliezer ben Jacob says, the daughter of proselytes should not marry into the priesthood unless her mother be from Israel” They all interpret the same verse (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 44:22" href="/Ezekiel.44.22"><i>Ez</i>. 44:22</a>): “Only virgins from the seed of the House of Israel.” Rebbi Jehudah says, unless his father be from Israel. Rebbi Eliezer ben Jacob says, either her father or her mother. Rebbi Yose says, unless they are born in the holiness of Israel. Rebbi Simeon says, unless they grow the hymen in the holiness of Israel. It was stated in the name of Rebbi Simeon: “A girl which became a proselyte being less than three years and one day of age is acceptable for the priesthood since it was said (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 31:18" href="/Numbers.31.18"><i>Num</i>. 31:18</a>): ‘All the female children unfit for sleeping with a male you shall let live for yourselves,’ and Phineas was with them.” How do the rabbis explain? You shall let live as slaves and slave girls for yourselves.
Rebbi Yose, Rebbi Yasa in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan; Rebbi Jonah, Rebbi Ḥiyya in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: Practice follows Rebbi Yose. Ḥanin bar Abba in the name of Rav: Practice follows Rebbi Yose, but Cohanim are used to follow Rebbi Eliezer ben Jacob. A Cohen married the daughter of proselytes. The case came before Rebbi Abbahu who let him kneel before the low bench. Rebbi Bevai said to him, did the Rabbi not teach us that practice follows Rebbi Yose? He answered, but are not Cohanim used to follow Rebbi Eliezer ben Jacob? He retorted, Rebbi, does one whip because of what one is used to do? He said to him, if you look at it in such a way, you have appeased me and I shall let him get up. After he got up, he said to him, since the lash was withdrawn I am permitted to have her.
Rebbi Jacob bar Idi in the name of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi: It happened that a family in the South had a bad reputation. Rebbi sent Romanus to investigate them. He investigated and found that a grandmother had been converted at less than three years and a day of age, and he declared them fit for the priesthood. Rav Hoshaia said, he declared them fit following Rebbi Simeon. Rebbi Ze‘ira said, here it is everybody’s opinion since Rebbi Ze‘ira said in the name of Rav Ada bar Ahava, Rebbi Judan brings it in the name of Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: The child of an adult is fit since it is a prohibition deduced from a positive commandment. (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 21:13" href="/Leviticus.21.13"><i>Lev</i>. 21:13</a>) “But he shall take a wife in her virginity.” Any prohibition deduced from a positive commandment is a positive commandment. Analogously, (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 21:14" href="/Leviticus.21.14"><i>Lev</i>. 21:14</a>) “only a virgin from amidst his people he shall take as wife,” not a proselyte. Is any prohibition deduced from a positive commandment a positive commandment? Rebbi Hoshaia objected: But the second generation of an Egyptian is a prohibition deduced from a positive commandment! Rebbi Hoshaia turned around and said, a positive commandment for Israel cannot be compared to a positive commandment for Cohanim. A positive commandment for Israel implies a prohibition for everybody. A positive commandment for Cohanim implies a prohibition for Cohanim but a permission for Levites and Israel.

Halakhah 7

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> If somebody says, this my son is a bastard, he cannot be believed<sup class="footnote-marker">179</sup><i class="footnote">Since a father is a relative of his wife’s child, he is unable to testify about him.</i>. Even if both of them say about the fetus in her belly that he is a bastard, they cannot be believed<sup class="footnote-marker">180</sup><i class="footnote">Both parents agree. They cannot testify even before the child’s birth when the child does not yet have a personality in the legal sense that the formal rules of testimony would be applicable to him.</i>. Rebbi Jehudah says, they are believed<sup class="footnote-marker">181</sup><i class="footnote">Even the father alone is able to declare his son illegitimate by the power invested in him by <a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 21:17" href="/Deuteronomy.21.17"><i>Deut</i>. 21:17</a>.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “If somebody says, this my son is a bastard, he cannot be believed,” etc. There, we have stated<sup class="footnote-marker">182</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Bava Batra 8:7:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Bava_Batra.8.7.1">Mishnah <i>Baba batra</i> 8:8</a>, dealing with rights of inheritance.</i>: “If somebody said, this is my son, he is to be believed.” Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: To give him<sup class="footnote-marker">183</sup><i class="footnote">Make him a legal heir.</i>, but not to take from him. Rebbi Yose said, is that not the Mishnah: “Even if both of them say about the fetus in her belly that he is a bastard, they cannot be believed”<sup class="footnote-marker">184</sup><i class="footnote">The Mishnah makes the statement of R. Joḥanan superfluous.</i>? Maybe it<sup class="footnote-marker">185</sup><i class="footnote">The statement of R. Abbahu in the name of R. Joḥanan.</i> was said following Rebbi Jehudah, for Rebbi Jehudah said, they can be believed; Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: To give him, but not to take from him. Rebbi Ḥizqiah said, still it is a <i>baraita</i>: “For he has to recognize the firstborn, the son of the hated one.<sup class="footnote-marker">186</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 21:17" href="/Deuteronomy.21.17"><i>Deut</i>. 21:17</a>. Quoting a verse is obviously not quoting a <i>baraita</i>. Probably the <i>baraita</i> quoted in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 78b" href="/Kiddushin.78b">Babli, 78b</a>, <i>Sifry Deut</i>. 217 is meant: “ ‘For he has to recognize the firstborn, the son of the hated one;’ he has to make him recognized by others; this implies that a person is believed if he says, this son of mine is the firstborn. Rebbi Jehudah says, just as a man is believed if he says, this son of mine is the firstborn, so he is believed if he says that he is the son of a divorcee or one who had received <i>ḥalîṣah</i>, but the Sages say, he is not believed.”</i>” If they<sup class="footnote-marker">187</sup><i class="footnote">The parents.</i> maintained that he was his son but at the moment of his death he said that he was not his son, he cannot be believed<sup class="footnote-marker">188</sup><i class="footnote">Once a person has obtained public recognition as a son, the presumption of permanence of the <i>status quo ante</i> requires valid testimony by two independent witnesses to change that status; cf. <i>Giṭṭin</i> Chapter 3.</i>. That he was not his son but at the moment of his death he said that he was his son, he is believed<sup class="footnote-marker">189</sup><i class="footnote">Since the dying person also could have given an unrelated person a part of his estate.</i>. Some Tannaïm state on the first case that he is believed.
