Rebbi Ḥisqiah, Rebbi Zeriqan in the name of Rebbi Huna: If they maintained that he was from his slave girl, he is believed<sup class="footnote-marker">190</sup><i class="footnote">If the father acknowledged that he had fathered the child with his slave girl and everybody assumed that he had manumitted the pregnant girl in order to be the legal father of the child but on his deathbed he acknowledged that he never manumitted the girl and, therefore, his child is not his child in Jewish law (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yevamot 2:5:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yevamot.2.5.1">Mishnah <i>Yebamot</i> 2:5</a>), he must be believed since his statement now is compatible with his earlier statements.</i>. If he was standing next to the customs collectors<sup class="footnote-marker">191</sup><i class="footnote">When he would have to pay customs duty for the importation of a slave but not for an accompanying son.</i> and said, he is my son, but later he said, he is my slave, he is believed<sup class="footnote-marker">192</sup><i class="footnote">We believe him that he was cheating on the customs.</i>. He is my slave, but later he said, he is my son, he is not believed<sup class="footnote-marker">193</sup><i class="footnote">Nobody pays custom duties which he is not obligated for.</i>. Some Tannaïm state, he is believed. Rebbi Mana said, because of those Samaritans<sup class="footnote-marker">194</sup><i class="footnote">In <i>Baba batra</i>: The Nabateans.</i> who use their sons as slaves.
It was stated<sup class="footnote-marker">195</sup><i class="footnote">According to the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Kiddushin (Lieberman) 5:5" href="/Tosefta_Kiddushin_(Lieberman).5.5">Tosephta, 5:5</a>, the author of this statement is R. Jehudah.</i>: He is believed about the adult but is not believed about the young<sup class="footnote-marker">196</sup><i class="footnote">It is clear that this sentence is corrupt and one must read: He is believed about the young but is not believed about the adult. Even R. Jehudah will agree that the Torah gives the father only the right to recognize or to refuse to recognize his child; the moment other people are involved, the usual rules of judicial proof must apply. Since the father does not have the right to declare his grandchildren as bastards, he has lost the right to declare his child a bastard the moment the child has children.</i>. Who is adult? Rebbi Ze‘ira said, any one who has a wife and children; Rebbi Abbahu, any one who has a wife<sup class="footnote-marker">197</sup><i class="footnote">Since by declaring his son a bastard, the father would forbid the son to his daughter-in-law, he would infringe upon the rights of a third party and cannot be believed.</i>. A <i>baraita</i><sup class="footnote-marker">198</sup><i class="footnote">Also quoted in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yevamot 47b" href="/Yevamot.47b">Babli, <i>Yebamot</i> 47b</a>.</i> disagrees with Rebbi Abbahu: A proselyte who was circumcised but did not immerse himself<sup class="footnote-marker">199</sup><i class="footnote">He is Jewish for R. Jehudah but still Gentile for R. Yose.</i> but has children; if he said, I was circumcised but did not immerse, he is believed and one immerses him even on the Sabbath because of parsimony<sup class="footnote-marker">200</sup><i class="footnote">To avoid problems with handling food when he or his family are present. Since for R. Yose, immersion of a circumcised proselyte changes him from Gentile to Jew, this could not be done on the Sabbath. One has to assume that the father admitted that he never was immersed only after he and his children already were known as Jews. Then he can no longer testify to disqualify his children from prospective Jewish marriages; he must be accepted as a Jew.</i>, the words of Rav<sup class="footnote-marker">201</sup><i class="footnote">This certainly must read “Rebbi” since the Babylonian Amora Rav Jehudah cannot be the author of a <i>baraita</i>.</i> Jehudah. What does Rebbi Abbahu do with this<sup class="footnote-marker">202</sup><i class="footnote">Since the <i>baraita</i> implies that one immerses him on the Sabbath only because he has children; does this not prove R. Ze‘ira’s point?</i>? He explains it, because who cares<sup class="footnote-marker">203</sup><i class="footnote">Since the author of the <i>baraita</i> is R. Jehudah for whom immersion is unnecessary, there is no problem of Sabbath desecration involved and he will agree that in order to satisfy even the followers of R. Yose, the proselyte should immerse himself at the first opportunity. This explanation is attributed to R. Jehudah himself in the Babli, <i>loc</i>.<i>cit</i>.</i>?

Halakhah 8

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> If somebody empowered his agent to contract preliminary marriage for his daughter and then went himself and contracted for her, ifhe was first, his preliminary marriage is valid<sup class="footnote-marker">204</sup><i class="footnote">Appointing an agent does not abolish the intrinsic right of a father to contract for his underage daughter’s marriage (to a different person).</i>, but if his agent was first, that preliminary marriage is valid<sup class="footnote-marker">205</sup><i class="footnote">If the father himself would marry his daughter successively to two different men, the second marriage would be nonexistent. The actions of father and agent can be considered as if all were actions of the father himself.</i>. If precedence cannot be established, both give a bill of divorce or, if they agree, one gives a bill of divorce and one marries definitively.<br>Similarly, if a woman empowered her agent to contract preliminary marriage for her and then went and contracted for herself, if she was first, her preliminary marriage is valid<sup class="footnote-marker">204</sup><i class="footnote">Appointing an agent does not abolish the intrinsic right of a father to contract for his underage daughter’s marriage (to a different person).</i>, but if her agent’s was first, that preliminary marriage is valid<sup class="footnote-marker">205</sup><i class="footnote">If the father himself would marry his daughter successively to two different men, the second marriage would be nonexistent. The actions of father and agent can be considered as if all were actions of the father himself.</i>. If precedence cannot be established, both give a bill of divorce or, if they agree, one gives a bill of divorce and one marries definitively.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “Similarly, if a woman empowered her agent,” etc. <sup class="footnote-marker">219</sup><i class="footnote">Since the argument is repeated for Mishnah 9, it is clear that the Halakhah refers both to Mishnah 8 and Mishnah 9. The statement of R. Joḥanan is in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Gittin 4:1:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Gittin.4.1.2"><i>Giṭṭin</i> 4:1</a>, see <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Kiddushin 4:1:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Kiddushin.4.1.1">Notes 2–3</a> there for explanation.</i> Does this not disagree with Rebbi Joḥanan, since Rebbi Joḥanan said that a person invalidates agency by a declaration? He explains it by the stringency of the rules of adultery and incest. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun understood this from the latter part: “Similarly, if a woman empowered her agent to contract preliminary marriage for her and then went and contracted for herself.” Does this not disagree with Rebbi Joḥanan, since Rebbi Joḥanan said that a person invalidates agency by a declaration? He explains it by the stringency of the rules of adultery and incest.

Halakhah 9

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> If somebody left for overseas together with his wife; he returns with his wife and her children and says, “the wife with whom I left for overseas is this one and those are her children,”<sup class="footnote-marker">220</sup><i class="footnote">A Cohen who wants to find matches for his children as members of the priestly clan.</i> he does not have to bring proof either about the wife<sup class="footnote-marker">221</sup><i class="footnote">Even if nobody recognizes her anymore.</i> or the children. “She died and those are her children,” he has to bring proof about the children<sup class="footnote-marker">222</sup><i class="footnote">That they are the children of his legal wife.</i> but not about the wife.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “If somebody left for overseas together with his wife,” etc. Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: They considered a man and his wife as two witnesses<sup class="footnote-marker">224</sup><i class="footnote">In order to let a person marry a Jewish partner, the court will need to have either generally accepted knowledge that the person is Jewish and is not a bastard, or to require testimony to this effect. A man and his wife are really barred from testifying about their children but since a woman is not supposed to raise another woman’s children as her own, her assertion can be believed.</i> since it is general knowledge that a woman will not be silent about another woman’s children. Rebbi Abun referred this to the later statement: “I married a wife overseas, this is she and those are her children;” Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: They considered a man and his wife as two witnesses since it is general knowledge that a woman will not be silent about another woman’s children<sup class="footnote-marker">225</sup><i class="footnote">Therefore, once the foreign woman has been accepted as his legitimate wife, no proof is needed about the children. In the language of the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Kiddushin (Lieberman) 5:8" href="/Tosefta_Kiddushin_(Lieberman).5.8">Tosephta (5:8</a>): “A woman is believed if she says: These are my children.”</i>.

Halakhah 10

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> “I married a wife overseas, this is she and those are her children,” he has to bring proof about the wife<sup class="footnote-marker">223</sup><i class="footnote">That she is of those whom he legally could marry.</i> but not about her children. “She died and those are her children,” he has bring proof both about the wife and about the children.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">206</sup><i class="footnote">In the ms. but not in <i>editio princeps</i>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Kiddushin 4:10:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Kiddushin.4.10.2">Halakhah 8</a> follows <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Kiddushin 4:9:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Kiddushin.4.9.2">Halakhah 10</a>. The theme of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Kiddushin 4:10:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Kiddushin.4.10.2">Halakhah 8</a> agrees better with Mishnah 10 than with Mishnah 8.</i> “If somebody empowered his agent,” etc. It was stated: “If a man and a woman come from overseas; he says, she is my wife, and she says, he is my husband. One will not execute anybody because of her being a married woman<sup class="footnote-marker">207</sup><i class="footnote">If somebody commits adultery with the woman, he cannot be prosecuted in the absence of proof (by witnesses or documents) that the woman actually is a wife, not a concubine.</i>. If they become generally known<sup class="footnote-marker">208</sup><i class="footnote">Public knowledge creates <i>prima facie</i> evidence which is valid as long as it is not rebutted by legal proof to the contrary; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Ketubot 5:4:3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Ketubot.5.4.3"><i>Ketubot</i> 5:5, Note 100</a>.</i>, one will execute because of her being a married woman.” How long does it take to be generally known? Rebbi Jonah, Rebbi Abba, Rebbi Ḥiyya in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: Up to thirty days<sup class="footnote-marker">209</sup><i class="footnote">Once a couple has lived in town as husband and wife for thirty days, adultery by another man with the wife is a capital crime since it seems unlikely that she would be able to prove that she is not married. Once <i>prima facie</i> evidence is established, husband and wife are barred from testifying in the matter since they are presumed related to each other.</i>. There<sup class="footnote-marker">210</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Tahorot 3:8" href="/Mishnah_Tahorot.3.8">Mishnah <i>Ṭahorot</i> 3:8</a>.</i>, we have stated: “A toddler who is found near cake-dough with a piece of dough in his hand<sup class="footnote-marker">211</sup><i class="footnote">The dough is supposed to be made in the purity of heave. The toddler is assumed to be impure unless he was immersed in a <i>miqweh</i> and then watched every moment lest he touch anything which would make him impure. If the toddler took the cake dough by himself, the cake dough is impure. If it is known that he was handed the piece of dough by a pure adult, the rest of the cake dough remains pure.</i>, Rebbi Meïr declares pure<sup class="footnote-marker">212</sup><i class="footnote">R. Meïr is reluctant to accept that anything which happens most of the time happens all the time unless the contrary be known. Since some toddlers do not touch anything impure and some toddlers do not play with dough if they see it, it is not said that the cake dough has to be impure.</i> but the Sages declare it impure, for toddlers will slap their hands on cake-dough<sup class="footnote-marker">213</sup><i class="footnote">The cake dough is impure by <i>prima facie</i> evidence unless proven to be otherwise.</i>.” Does one burn because of general knowledge<sup class="footnote-marker">214</sup><i class="footnote">If the cake dough was made of heave material.</i>? Rebbi Yose in the name of Rebbi Ze‘ira: Rebbi Joḥanan and Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish disagree. Rebbi Joḥanan said, one executes because of general knowledge. Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said, one does not execute because of general knowledge. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun in the name of Rebbi Ze‘ira: Everybody agrees that one executes because of general knowledge. Where do they disagree? About burning. Rebbi Joḥanan said, one executes because of general knowledge but one does not burn because of general knowledge<sup class="footnote-marker">215</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 80a" href="/Kiddushin.80a">Babli 80a</a>; cf. also <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Demai 6:5:3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Demai.6.5.3"><i>Demay</i> 6:6, Note 138</a>.</i>. Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said, since one executes because of general knowledge, one also burns because of general knowledge. And from where that one executes because of general knowledge? Rebbi Samuel, the son of Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">216</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Ex</i>.. 21:15.</i>: “He who hits his father or his mother shall be put to death.” But is it certain that this one is his father? Is it not only general knowledge that he is his father<sup class="footnote-marker">217</sup><i class="footnote">This is not really a proof since fatherhood is not only a matter of public knowledge but also of probability since “most intercourse of an adulteress is still with her husband” (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sotah 1:7:4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sotah.1.7.4"><i>Soṭah</i>, Yerushalmi 1:7 Note 265</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 27a" href="/Kiddushin.27a">Babli 27a</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Yevamot (Lieberman) 12:8" href="/Tosefta_Yevamot_(Lieberman).12.8">Tosephta <i>Yebamot</i> 12:8</a>.)</i>? But it says, one executes. So here also<sup class="footnote-marker">218</sup><i class="footnote">In the matter of the couple who married at another place and declare themselves husband and wife; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 80a" href="/Kiddushin.80a">Babli 80a</a>.</i> one executes.
“ “I married a wife overseas.” It was stated: If he brought proof about the older ones<sup class="footnote-marker">226</sup><i class="footnote">If the wife had died.</i>, he still has to bring proof about the younger ones. Why? Rebbi Jonah said, I say that perhaps she was divorced in the meantime<sup class="footnote-marker">227</sup><i class="footnote">They could be children of the same woman but the older ones would be priests, the younger ones desecrated as children of a divorcee married to a priest. The <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 79b" href="/Kiddushin.79b">Babli, 79b</a>, disagrees and holds that once the wife has been found acceptable for the priesthood, no proof about her children is needed. It refers “older” and “younger” to children from different mothers.</i>.

Halakhah 11

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> One man should not be alone with two women<sup class="footnote-marker">228</sup><i class="footnote">In a locked room.</i> but one woman may be alone with two men. Rebbi Simeon says, he may be alone with two women as long as his wife is with him; he can sleep with them in a hostelry<sup class="footnote-marker">229</sup><i class="footnote">Where everybody sleeps in the same room.</i> because his wife will watch over him. A man can be alone with his mother or his daughter and sleep with them with their skins touching; once they grew up each one sleeps in his garment.<br>And a bachelor shall not be a school teacher<sup class="footnote-marker">230</sup><i class="footnote">Because of the mothers of the schoolchildren.</i>; a woman shall not be a school teacher. Rebbi Eliezer says, also a man without a wife shall not be a school teacher.<sup class="footnote-marker">231</sup><i class="footnote">If he is married but his wife lives at another place, he is considered unmarried in this respect.</i><br>Rebbi Jehudah says, a bachelor shall not be a shepherd and two bachelors shall not sleep under one cover, but the Sages permit<sup class="footnote-marker">232</sup><i class="footnote">They hold that Jews never engage in bestiality or homosexual acts.</i>.<br>Anybody whose occupation is with women should never be alone with women. And a man should not teach his son a craft for women.<br>Rebbi Meïr says that a man should try to teach his son a clean and easy trade and pray to Him to Whom riches and properties belong since there is no trade in which poverty and riches are not found, for neither poverty nor riches come from the trade. Rebbi Simeon<sup class="footnote-marker">233</sup><i class="footnote">This list is different in different Mishnah mss. It seems that both “hairdresser” and “potter” should be deleted and replaced by קָרָר or קָרָן “teamster”. But the text could also be a conflation of two different texts, one denigrating trades that have a reputation of dishonesty and one that serves women (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 82a" href="/Kiddushin.82a">Babli 82a</a>) like jewelers, hairdressers, etc. For a better text cf. below, 66c 1. 26.</i> ben Eleazar says, did you ever see a wild animal or a bird which had a trade? And they sustain themselves without pain. But they were created only to serve me and sustain themselves without pain, and I was created to serve my Maker, it should be logical that I should be able to sustain myself without pain; only I worsened my deeds and destroyed my sustenance.<br>Abba Gorion from Sidon says in the name of Abba Shaul<sup class="footnote-marker">234</sup><i class="footnote">In the Babli: Abba Guria.</i>: A man should not teach his son to be a donkey driver, a camel driver, a hairdresser, a sailor, a potter, a shepherd, or a grocer, since their occupations are those of robbers. Rebbi Jehudah says in the latter’s name: Most donkey drivers are wicked<sup class="footnote-marker">235</sup><i class="footnote">They are always hitting their animal.</i>, most camel drivers are in order<sup class="footnote-marker">236</sup><i class="footnote">Camels will walk by themselves a certain number of steps and have to be led gently.</i>, most sailors are pious; the best of physicians goes to hell<sup class="footnote-marker">237</sup><i class="footnote">He will be punished for every patient of his who dies because he did not give him the best of care.</i>, the qualified among the butchers is an associate of Amaleq<sup class="footnote-marker">238</sup><i class="footnote">He is a professional killer.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “One man should not be alone with two women,” etc. Rebbi Abun said, when has this been said<sup class="footnote-marker">239</sup><i class="footnote">That a woman can be alone with two men.</i>? With decent men. But with profligates she should not be alone even with a hundred men<sup class="footnote-marker">240</sup><i class="footnote">In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 80b" href="/Kiddushin.80b">Babli, 80b</a>, this is a statement of Rav Jehudah in the name of Rav.</i>. It was stated<sup class="footnote-marker">241</sup><i class="footnote">A similar text is quoted in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 80b" href="/Kiddushin.80b">Babli, 80b</a>.</i>: A one day old child who died is for his father, his mother, and all his relatives like one fully grown<sup class="footnote-marker">242</sup><i class="footnote">They have to observe all the rules of the impurity of the dead and of mourning.</i>. Not only if he died when one day old but even if he was alive when his head and most of his body were born<sup class="footnote-marker">243</sup><i class="footnote">From the moment his life is independent and it is no longer permitted to destroy the fetus to save the mother’s life (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Oholot 7:6" href="/Mishnah_Oholot.7.6">Mishnah <i>Ahilut</i> 7:6</a>).</i>. He is carried out at the bosom<sup class="footnote-marker">244</sup><i class="footnote">He does not need a bier and ten adults like a grown-up. Since he died before he had occasion to sin, his soul is pure and ready to enter Paradise without human intercession.</i> and buried by one woman and two men; Abba Shaul says even one man and two women. It is obvious that Rebbi Simeon will agree with Abba Shaul but Abba Shaul does not need to agree with Rebbi Simeon since there is no sexual desire in the cemetery<sup class="footnote-marker">245</sup><i class="footnote">In all other situations, Abba Shaul agrees with the anonymous Tanna. In the Babli, Abba Shaul’s statement is rejected by reference to a story which R. Ḥananel (quoted by <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosafot on Kiddushin 15a:12:1" href="/Tosafot_on_Kiddushin.15a.12.1">Tosaphot <i>s</i>.<i>v</i>. כי</a>) identifies as that of The Widow of Ephesus.</i>.
Rebbi Joḥanan in the name of Rebbi Simeon ben Ioḥai<sup class="footnote-marker">246</sup><i class="footnote">So also in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sotah 1:1:8" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sotah.1.1.8"><i>Soṭah</i> 1:1, Note 38</a>. In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 80b" href="/Kiddushin.80b">Babli 80b</a>, R. Joḥanan in the name of R. Ismael, in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sanhedrin 21b" href="/Sanhedrin.21b"><i>Sanhedrin</i> 21b</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Avodah Zarah 36b" href="/Avodah_Zarah.36b"><i>Avodah zarah</i> 36b</a>, in the name of R. Simeon ben Yoṣadaq. The latter attribution probably is the correct one; in these two quotes also the verse correctly is called “a hint”, not a proof.</i>: “If your brother, your mother’s son, or your son, or your daughter incites you<sup class="footnote-marker">247</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 13:7" href="/Deuteronomy.13.7"><i>Deut</i>. 13:7</a>. As usual, the reference is to the part of the verse not quoted; in this case that the inciting happens “in secret”.</i>”. “Your mother in secret,” “your daughter in secret.” A man can be alone with his mother and live with her<sup class="footnote-marker">248</sup><i class="footnote">In a one-room apartment.</i>, with his daughter and live with her, with his sister and does not live with her, and sleep with them with their skins touching. Rebbi Ḥalaphta ben Shaul stated: The daughter with her father up to the age of three years and one day<sup class="footnote-marker">249</sup><i class="footnote">The day she becomes nubile.</i>; the son with his mother up to the age of nine years and one day<sup class="footnote-marker">250</sup><i class="footnote">Before that day, his sex act has no legal consequences (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yevamot 10:5:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yevamot.10.5.1">Mishnah <i>Yebamot</i> 10:6</a>).</i>. If they get older, each one sleeps in his own clothing. It was stated<sup class="footnote-marker">251</sup><i class="footnote">Similar statements are in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Berakhot 24a" href="/Berakhot.24a"><i>Berakhot</i> 24a</a>.</i>: If two people sleep in the same bed, each one covers himself with his own garment and recites {the <i>Šema‘</i>}<sup class="footnote-marker">252</sup><i class="footnote">Which, as a holy text, it is forbidden to recite in the presence of nudity.</i>; if his son or daughter were small it is permitted. There, they say: A man with his wife is permitted<sup class="footnote-marker">253</sup><i class="footnote">Even if both are naked under the same bedsheet, since “his wife is part of his body” (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Berakhot 24a" href="/Berakhot.24a">Babli <i>Berakhot</i> 24a</a>).</i>. Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa in the name of Rebbi Eleazar: A man with his wife is problematic<sup class="footnote-marker">254</sup><i class="footnote">Even if his wife is part of his body, he could recite the <i>Šema‘</i> while lying close to her only if she would not represent a sexual attraction to him. This is not a desirable situation.</i>.
New paragraph. “And a bachelor shall not be a school teacher; a woman shall not be a school teacher, etc.” It was stated: Rebbi Eliezer says, also a man with a wife and children shall not be a school teacher if they are not with him at that place. Rebbi Yudan ben Rebbi Ismael acted accordingly in the case of a Mishnah teacher.
New paragraph. “Rebbi Jehudah says, a bachelor shall not be a shepherd and two bachelors shall not sleep under one cover, but the Sages permit.” Does not Rebbi Jehudah say it correctly? What is the rabbi’s reason? Perish the thought! Jews are not suspected either with males or with animals. But did we not state: “A bachelor shall not be a school teacher”<sup class="footnote-marker">255</sup><i class="footnote">Suspecting the unmarried school teacher to be a pedophile with young males.</i>? Because his mother or his sister will come with him<sup class="footnote-marker">256</sup><i class="footnote">He is only suspected to be susceptible to the lure of heterosexual relations. The same argument is in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 82a" href="/Kiddushin.82a">Babli, 82a</a>, where also it is indicated that a female school teacher is not suspected of being attracted to her male students but to their fathers.</i>.
New paragraph. “A man should not teach his son a craft for women,” etc. It was stated: A man should not teach his son to be a donkey driver, a camel driver, a sailor, a potter, a teamster, a shepherd, or a grocer, since their occupations are those of robbers<sup class="footnote-marker">233</sup><i class="footnote">This list is different in different Mishnah mss. It seems that both “hairdresser” and “potter” should be deleted and replaced by קָרָר or קָרָן “teamster”. But the text could also be a conflation of two different texts, one denigrating trades that have a reputation of dishonesty and one that serves women (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 82a" href="/Kiddushin.82a">Babli 82a</a>) like jewelers, hairdressers, etc. For a better text cf. below, 66c 1. 26.</i>.
New paragraph. Abba Orion from Sidon says in the name of Abba Shaul<sup class="footnote-marker">234</sup><i class="footnote">In the Babli: Abba Guria.</i>: Most donkey drivers are wicked<sup class="footnote-marker">235</sup><i class="footnote">They are always hitting their animal.</i>, most camel drivers are in order<sup class="footnote-marker">236</sup><i class="footnote">Camels will walk by themselves a certain number of steps and have to be led gently.</i>, most sailors are pious, most bastards are intelligent, most slaves are beautiful, most children of reputed parents are bashful, most sons look like their mother’s brothers. The qualified physicians go to hell<sup class="footnote-marker">237</sup><i class="footnote">He will be punished for every patient of his who dies because he did not give him the best of care.</i>, the qualified among the butchers is an associate of Amaleq<sup class="footnote-marker">238</sup><i class="footnote">He is a professional killer.</i>. Rebbi Simeon ben Ioḥai stated: Kill the best of Gentiles<sup class="footnote-marker">257</sup><i class="footnote">He spent 14 years in a cave on the run from the Roman government. In <i>Mekhilta dR</i>.<i>Ismael</i>,<i>Bešallaḥ</i> 1; <i>Mekhilta dR</i>.<i>Simeon bar Ioḥai</i> p. 51; <i>Tanḥuma Bešallaḥ</i>8, his proof is from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 14:7" href="/Exodus.14.7"><i>Ex</i>. 14:7</a>, where Pharao mobilized 600 chariots and it is argued that the horses to draw the chariots must have belonged to “those who feared the word of the Eternal” (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 9:20" href="/Exodus.9.20"><i>Ex</i>. 9:20</a>); but that verse refers only to domestic animals which at that time did not include horses used only by the military.</i>, smash the head of the best of snakes; the best qualified among women is a sorceress. Blessed is he who does the will of the Omnipresent.
Rebbi Meïr says<sup class="footnote-marker">258</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Kiddushin (Lieberman) 5:14" href="/Tosefta_Kiddushin_(Lieberman).5.14">Tosephta 5:14</a>.</i>: A person can earn his livelihood from anywhere. Blessed is he who sees his parents in an esteemed trade; woe to him who sees his parents in a degrading<sup class="footnote-marker">259</sup><i class="footnote">In G: despised.</i> trade.
New paragraph. “Rebbi Meïr says that a man should try to teach his son a clean trade,” etc. What should a man do? A person should try and teach his son an unassuming trade and pray for mercy to Him to Whom riches belong since there is no trade in which poor and rich people are not found, for everything depends on a person’s merit. <sup class="footnote-marker">260</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Kiddushin (Lieberman) 5:15" href="/Tosefta_Kiddushin_(Lieberman).5.15">Tosephta 5:15</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 82b" href="/Kiddushin.82b">Babli 82b</a>.</i> Rebbi Simeon ben Eleazar in the name of Rebbi Meïr: Did you ever see a lion porter, a (lion) [deer]<sup class="footnote-marker">261</sup><i class="footnote">Reading of G and the parallel sources.</i> maker of fig cakes, a fox grocer, a wolf selling pots? And they sustain themselves without pain. Why were they created? Only to serve me, and I was created to serve my Maker. Is it not an argument <i>de minore ad maius</i>? Since they were created to serve me and sustain themselves so without pain, should it not be logical that I, who was created to serve my Maker, should be able to sustain myself without pain? What caused me to have to sustain myself with pain? One has to say, my sins. Because I worsened my deeds and destroyed my sustenance.

Halakhah 12

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Rebbi Nehorai says: I am leaving aside all trades in the world and teach my son only Torah<sup class="footnote-marker">262</sup><i class="footnote">This really is frowned upon, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pirkei Avot 2:2" href="/Pirkei_Avot.2.2">Mishnah <i>Avot</i> 2:2</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pirkei Avot 4:5" href="/Pirkei_Avot.4.5">4:5</a>.</i>, for a man eats from its rewards in this world and the capital remains for the future world. But with other trades it is not so, for if a person is afflicted with sickness, or old age, or a measure of suffering, and cannot continue in his trade, he dies, abandoned, from hunger. But the Torah is different, it guards him from all evil in his youth and gives him a future and hope in his old age. What does it say about his youth? “Those who trust in the Eternal will renew strength, they rise on wings like an eagle, they run without effort, they walk without tiring.<sup class="footnote-marker">263</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 40:31" href="/Isaiah.40.31"><i>Is</i>. 40:31</a>.</i>” What does it say about his old age? “They still bear fruit in old age, fat and invigorated they will be.<sup class="footnote-marker">264</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 92:15" href="/Psalms.92.15"><i>Ps</i>. 92:15</a>.</i>” So it says about our father Abraham, peace on him: “Abraham was old, came into days, and the Eternal blessed Abraham with everything.<sup class="footnote-marker">265</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 24:1" href="/Genesis.24.1"><i>Gen</i>. 24:1</a>.</i>” We find that our father Abraham kept the entire Torah before it was given, as it is said: “As a reward because Abraham listened to My voice and kept My watch, My commandments, My laws, and My teachings.<sup class="footnote-marker">266</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 26:5" href="/Genesis.26.5"><i>Gen</i>. 26:5</a>.</i>”
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">267</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Kiddushin (Lieberman) 5:16-17" href="/Tosefta_Kiddushin_(Lieberman).5.16-17">Tosephta 5:16–17</a>; a shortened version in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Kiddushin 82b" href="/Kiddushin.82b">Babli, 82b</a>, and <i>Masekhet Sopherim</i> 17:1.</i>“Rebbi Nehorai says: I am leaving aside all trades in the world and teach my son only Torah.” For all trades support a person only in his youth as long as he is in possession of his powers. But if a person is afflicted with sickness or a measure of suffering, and cannot continue working, he dies from hunger. But the Torah is different, it honors him and guards him from all evil in his youth and gives him a future and hope in his old age<sup class="footnote-marker">268</sup><i class="footnote">G has here an amplification that looks redundant.</i>. What does it say about his youth? “Those who trust in the Eternal will renew strength, they rise on wings like an eagle, they run without effort, they walk without tiring.<sup class="footnote-marker">263</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 40:31" href="/Isaiah.40.31"><i>Is</i>. 40:31</a>.</i>” What does it say about his old age? “They still bear fruit in old age, fat and invigorated they will be.<sup class="footnote-marker">264</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 92:15" href="/Psalms.92.15"><i>Ps</i>. 92:15</a>.</i>” So you find about the patriarch Abraham who kept the Torah before it came into the world<sup class="footnote-marker">269</sup><i class="footnote">G lacks “into the world”. The text of L should be interpreted as “came into <i>this</i> world”, not excluding the doctrine of pre-existence of the Torah in the abstract prior to Creation.</i>, as it is said: “As a reward because Abraham listened to My voice and kept My watch, My commandments, My laws, and My teachings.<sup class="footnote-marker">266</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 26:5" href="/Genesis.26.5"><i>Gen</i>. 26:5</a>.</i>” Also it made him great and blessed him in his youth and gave him a future and hope in his old age. What does it say about his youth? “Abraham was very wealthy with livestock, silver, and gold.” And about his old age, what does it say? “Abraham was old, came into days, and the Eternal blessed Abraham with everything.<sup class="footnote-marker">265</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 24:1" href="/Genesis.24.1"><i>Gen</i>. 24:1</a>.</i>”
Rebbi Ḥizqiah, Rebbi Cohen in the name of Rav. It is forbidden to dwell in a city which has neither a medical man, nor a public bath, nor a court lashing and jailing<sup class="footnote-marker">270</sup><i class="footnote">A different version is in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sanhedrin 17b" href="/Sanhedrin.17b">Babli, <i>Sanhedrin</i> 17b</a>.</i>. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, also it is forbidden to dwell in a city which has no vegetable garden<sup class="footnote-marker">271</sup><i class="footnote">In the Babli, this is a Tannaïtic statement attributed to R. Aqiba. A diet without fruit and vegetables is unhealthy.</i>. Rebbi Ḥizqiah, Rebbi Cohen in the name of Rav: Every person will have to justify himself for everything his eye saw and which he did not eat<sup class="footnote-marker">272</sup><i class="footnote">Since asceticism is sinful; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Nedarim 1:1:14" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Nedarim.1.1.14"><i>Nedarim</i> 1:1, Note 95</a>.</i>. Rebbi Eleazar took note of this statement and saved coins from which he ate every kind once a year.
